ESSENTIAL MEDICINES AND HEALTH SUPPLIES LIST FOR UGANDA (EMHSLU) 2023

> Published by the Ministry of Health Uganda First edition: 1997.
> Revised: November 2012, December 2016, September 2023.
>
> Any part of this document may be reproduced in any form without the
> prior permission of the publisher, provided that this is not for
> profit and that due acknowledgement is given.
>
> Any reproduction for profit must be given prior permission from the
> Ministry of Health.
>
> Copies may be obtained from:
>
> The Pharmacy Department, Ministry of Health Plot 6 Lourdel Road,
> P.O.Box 7272 Kampala, Uganda Tel: +256-417-771330
>
> Email: <ugandaclinicalguidelines@gmail.com>
>
> Website: [www.health.go.ug](http://www.health.go.ug/)
>
> Disclaimer
>
> Every effort has been made to ensure that the information in this book
> is accurate, complete, and conforms to the current therapeutic
> practice. However, the publisher, editor, and contributors cannot be
> held responsible for any errors, omissions, individual patient
> responses to recommended therapies, or other consequences that may
> arise from its use.

# FOREWORD

> **Dr. Aceng Jane Ruth Ocero**
>
> Hon. Minister of Health
>
> Pharmaceuticals play a very critical role in achieving the overall
> outcomes and goals related to the health sector. The National Health
> Policy, the National Medicines Policy, the Health Sector Strategic and
> Investment Plan III, and the National Pharmaceutical Sector Strategic
> Plan 2015-2020 emphasize the promotion of appropriate use of
> medicines, health and laboratory supplies.
>
> Appropriate use of medicines requires good diagnostic skills and
> access to well-performed laboratory services, good prescribing
> practices that follow clinical guidelines, good dispensing practices,
> and adherence to treatment by the patient. Very importantly,
> appropriate use requires the availability of essential medicines and
> health supplies (EMHS) at every service delivery point, combined with
> an efficient monitoring and evaluation system.
>
> The Essential Medicines and Health Supplies List for Uganda (EMHSLU)
> 2023 reflects the policy of the Ministry of Health, for the
> appropriate procurement of safe and efficacious essential medicines,
> health and laboratory supplies in public institutions.
>
> Like in the previous editions, all items have been categorised by the
> level of care, and also by the Vital, Essential and Necessary (VEN)
> classification.The VEN system prioritises items according to health
> impact, to ensure that adequate stock levels of life-saving medicines
> and health supplies at the facility will always be available, leading
> to better healthcare services for Ugandans.
>
> The EMHSLU 2023 was compiled based on recommendations from various
> categories of health workers at the Ministry of Health and from health
> facilities. It was updated in conjunction with the Uganda Clinical
> Guidelines (UCG) 2023, to ensure that all essential medicines, health
> and laboratory supplies needed to treat common conditions according to
> the UCG are included.
>
> It is the hope of the Ministry of Health that the updated essential
> medicines and health supplies list will be used by providers in both
> the public and private sectors, to guide, ensure availability and use
> of quality, safe, efficacious and cost-effective medicines, health and
> laboratory supplies in Uganda.
>
> I wish to thank all the members of the Ministry of Health Update Task
> Force, government parastatals, the medical consultants, district
> health workers, the private sector, the Uganda Reproductive Maternal
> Child and Adolescent Health Improvement Project (URMCHIP) and
> development partners.
>
> Finally, I thank the consultancy firm, Zenith Solutions Limited, that
> coordinated the overall inputs that led to the successful development
> of this book.

### Dr. Aceng Jane Ruth Ocero

> Hon. Minister of Health

![](media/image12.png)

> **10 EMHSLU**

# PREFACE

> **Dr. Henry G. Mwebesa** Director General of Health Services, Ministry
> of Health
>
> This fully updated publication replaces the EMHSLU 2016 and is being
> circulated to all public and private sector prescribers, pharmacists,
> training institutions, procurement agencies, warehouses, and
> regulatory authorities in the country.
>
> The Essential Medicines and Health Supplies List for Uganda (EMHSLU)
> 2023 is a list of safe, efficacious, and cost-effective medicines and
> health supplies that suit the healthcare needs of the majority of the
> Ugandan population.
>
> Access to essential medicines and health supplies is fundamental to
> ensuring equitable healthcare to the population. In addition,
> availability of proper diagnostic supplies and technologies ensures
> the appropriate use of these medicines and guarantees the overall
> quality of care received by the patients. In a resource-limited
> setting, the judicious use of supplies is required, and this EMHSLU
> provides a basis for efficient supply chain management, planning and
> procurement of supplies by the health facilities and procurement
> agencies.
>
> The EMHSLU 2023 follows the 2016 edition, and has been harmonized with
> the UCG 2023, so as to reflect medicines and diagnostic requirements
> for management of common conditions affecting the Ugandan population.
> Updating this edition was guided by a user survey that highlighted the
> usefulness, challenges and scope of the guidelines. This was followed
> by consultations from multiple stakeholders, to ensure comprehensive
> reviews, and was based on
>
> principles of clinical evidence-based medicine, cost-effectiveness,
> current WHO guidelines and Ministry of Health policies.
>
> The EMHSLU 2023 has maintained the previous arrangement of four
> sections i.e., essential medicines list, general health supplies list,
> specialist health supplies list, and the laboratory supplies list.
>
> The medicines list is classified by therapeutic categories, following
> the 22nd edition of the World Health Organisation (WHO) model list
> (2021), and contains both the general and specialist medicines in one
> list for ease of reference.
>
> The laboratory list developed in consultation with UNHLS includes
> standardized equipment and supplies, harmonized with the test
> techniques for each level of care within the health system, so as to
> ensure access to high quality, rapid, and affordable diagnostic tests
> for the care, treatment, prevention and surveillance of the conditions
> affecting the Ugandan population.
>
> In order to promote availability of medicines at all levels, all items
> in the EMHSLU 2023 have been classified by the "level of care" (L )
> corresponding to the competencies available at those levels, and also
> by the Vital, Essential and Necessary (VEN) criteria. During
> procurement, the vital (V) should be given priority over the
> 'essential' and 'necessary', as these are lifesaving and/or first line
> recommendations for the conditions, based on the available budgetary
> allocations.

![](media/image16.png)

> **EMHSLU 11**
>
> Access to essential medicines and health supplies is fundamen-tal to
> ensuring equitable healthcare to the population.
>
> Given the dynamic nature of therapeutics, the essential medicines and
> health supplies list needs to be regularly updated so as to maintain
> its credibility and relevance. Users are therefore encouraged to
> document and submit any recommendations that can improve future
> guidelines to the Ministry of Health.
>
> We hope that all health facilities will judiciously use the EMHSLU
> 2023, together with UCG 2023, and Practical Program Guidelines for
> Dispensing (PGD), to promote availability, affordability, appropriate
> use of resources and also to prevent negative consequences such as
> antimicrobial resistance and wastage of resources. It is further hoped
> that proper use of this guideline will improve the overall quality of
> health care in Uganda.

![](media/image20.png){width="1.7259350393700787in"
height="0.5572911198600174in"}

> Dr. Henry G. Mwebesa
>
> Director General of Health Services, Ministry of Health

# INTRODUCTION TO EMHSLU 2023

> *Essential Medicines Concept*
>
> In 1999, the World Health Organization Expert Committee on Essential
> Medicines defined essential medicines as those medicines that satisfy
> the healthcare needs of the majority of the population at a cost that
> is affordable to them and their community. Essential medicines should
> always be available, in adequate amounts, and in the appropriate
> dosage forms.
>
> The essential medicines concept is a public health principle that
> promotes efficient use of resources by establishing and using a
> limited list of carefully selected medicines. By selecting a few
> medicines, better treatment and easier supply, storage, and
> distribution can be assured at a lower cost. The concept is based on
> the observations that:

- The vast majority of health problems for most of the population can be
  treated with a small number of carefully selected medicines.

- In practice, most doctors and other health professionals routinely use
  fewer than 200 medicines; training and clinical experience should
  focus on the proper use of these medicines.

> *VEN classification*
>
> In the context of limited resources, it is very important to learn to
> prioritise medicines and health supplies. This is reflected by the
> Vital, Essential, Necessary (VEN) classification. Items are classified
> into three categories, according to their health impact:
>
> **V:** Vital items are used to diagnose and treat life-threatening
> conditions, or are considered medicine of choice or "first line" items
> in their therapeutic category.Their unavailability would cause serious
> harm and side effects.They must be ALWAYS available.
>
> **E:** Essential medicines are important; they are used to treat
> common illnesses, maybe less severe but nevertheless significant, or
> are second line items in their therapeutic categories.
>
> **N:** Necessary (or sometimes called non-essential) medicines are
> those used for minor or self-limiting illnesses, or diseases with less
> impact on the population, or items with a high cost for marginal
> therapeutic benefit.
>
> The VEN classification is intended to guide health facilities to
> prioritize items during procurement. Vital items have first priority,
> because their unavailability can lead to death of a patient or
> irreparable injury.
>
> Essential items have second priority; if these items are not
> available, the patient could suffer pain or great discomfort.
> Necessary items are needed and therefore on the order form; however,
> they have third priority.
>
> The VEN-classified EMHSLU also guides the National Medical Stores on
> which items to procure and which to include in the kits.
>
> VEN classification also allows for better and simplified stock, and
> storage management as a limited number of the most crucial items are
> available, which leads to better supply chain efficiency and
> effectiveness.
>
> *AWaRe classification*
>
> This applies to antimicrobial agents in relation to antimicrobial
> resistance.
>
> Products are classified in stewardship groups, namely, access, watch
> and reserve.
>
> *Access*
>
> Antibiotics with activities against commonly encountered susceptible
> pathogens and shows lower resistance potential than in other groups.
>
> *Watch*
>
> Antibiotics that have higher resistance potential include most of the
> highest priority agents among the critically important anti-microbial
> agents. They should be sparingly used to avoid potential resistance.
>
> *Reserve*
>
> These are antibiotics that should be reserved for treatment of
> confirmed or suspected infections due to multi-drug resistant
> organisms. Antibiotics in this group should be treated as last resort
> options.
>
> In this edition, effort has been made to avail them at a high specific
> level of care and patients.
>
> Prescribers are encouraged to take the AWaRe classification into
> consideration when prescribing antimicrobial agents. Availability of
> antimicrobial agents should be made at levels of care depending on
> prescriber competences. Their prescription and use should be guided by
> laboratory results.
>
> *Level of use (L)*
>
> The items in the EMHSLU 2023 have also been grouped according to level
> of use. Each item has a designation representing the lowest level of
> use. The item can be prescribed and dispensed at this level and all
> the levels above.This designation is in line with the diagnostic and
> clinical skills expected to be available
>
> []{#_bookmark6 .anchor}at that level. For specialist items, the use of
> an item is further restricted to facilities where a specific type of
> clinical and/or diagnostic expertise is available (e.g.,
> anti-cancers).
>
> The level indicated also guides procurement of health supplies by both
> the National Medical Stores and the health facilities.
>
> Below are the levels used in the list, including the highest
> professional cadre expected at lower-level health facilities.
>
> NR National referral hospital RR Regional referral hospital H Hospital
>
> HC4 Health centre 4 (Medical Officer) HC3 Health centre 3 (Clinical
> Officer)
>
> HC2 Health centre 2 (Enrolled Comprehensive Nurse)
>
> HC1 Health centre 1 (Community,VHT, CHEW)

# STRUCTURE OF EMHSLU 2023

> The EMHSLU 2023 comprises four sections, A-D.
>
> *Section A: Essential Medicines List 2023*
>
> This comprises both general use and specialist medicines. These have
> been classified by therapeutic categories following a similar
> structure to the 19th WHO Model List of Essential Medicines, 2021. It
> consists of all medicines recommended in the UCG 2023 that were
> selected based on efficacy, safety and cost-effectiveness.
>
> The specialist medicines are those for which specialized medical care,
> training, diagnosis or monitoring is needed. These are mostly
> restricted to regional and national referral hospitals where the
> required expertise is available.
>
> The relevant International Non-proprietary Name (INN) or generic names
> for the medicines are used throughout the list. Short forms of
> medicine names are used for only well-known abbreviations such AZT for
> zidovudine.
>
> This section is presented in tables labeled as: DS=dosage form, STR =
> strength, L = Level of use, C
>
> = VEN classification.
>
> *Section B: General Health Supplies*
>
> This section includes medical sundries used in all healthcare
> facilities and are arranged in alphabetical
>
> order.
>
> *Section C: Specialist Health Supplies*
>
> This list includes supplies used in specialized situations such as
> ophthalmology, dialysis, etc.
>
> *Section D: Laboratory Health Supplies*
>
> The laboratory list includes standardized equipment and supplies,
> harmonized with the test techniques, operating procedures for each
> type of test and for each level of care within the health system. The
> standardization is meant to strengthen the country's laboratory
> capacity and service delivery to provide access to high quality, rapid
> and affordable diagnostic tests for the care, treatment, prevention
> and surveillance of infectious and non-infectious diseases.
>
> The standardized laboratory list, which is also VEN-classified, helps
> to reduce the number of commodities being managed by the procurement
> bodies, leading to better supply chain management.

# COMPOSITION OF THE EMHSLU

> The EMHSLU 2023 comprises a total of 784 medicines, 738 health
> supplies and 1350 laboratory supplies, with 248%, 175% and 565% items
> classified as Vital on each list respectively.

# CHANGES TO THE EMHS-LU 2023

> A total of 35 medicines/formulations were deleted from the 2016
> Essential Medicine List for Uganda (EMLU) and 61 new medicines or
> formulations were included on the 2022 essential medicines list.The
> main reasons for deletion and addition of medicines were to align with
> the most current treatment guidelines, new disease patterns, evidence
> and/or development of new and better formulation or fixed dose
> combinations.
>
> New sections have been introduced to cater for n ewborn care items and
> covid-19 protective gear under the medical supplies, while section 8
> under the laboratory supplies caters for histology items for RRH and
> NRHs.
>
> *Essential medicines/formulations deleted from 2016 edition.*

1.  Moxifloxacin Tablet 400 mg

2.  Abacavir 60mg

3.  Abacavir sulfate 300mg

# AMENDMENTS

> Proposals for amendments to the EMHSLU 2023 with relevant arguments
> and literature should be sent to:
>
> Pharmacy Department, Ministry of Health Plot 6 Lourdel Road, P.O. Box
> 7272 Kampala, Uganda
>
> Tel: +256-417-771330, +256-417-712260,Toll
>
> Free; 0800100066
>
> Email: <ps@health.go.ug>:
>
> Website: [www.health.go.ug](http://www.health.go.ug/)
>
> Information to be included with an application for inclusion, change
> or deletion of a product in the
>
> EMHSLU.

- A summary statement of the proposal for

> inclusion, change or deletion.

- Name, address and contact details of the organization /individual
  consulted and/or supporting the application.

- International Non-proprietary Name (INN, generic name) of the medicine

- Formulation proposed for inclusion: state the relevant section or
  subsection, including adult and paediatric (if appropriate)

- International and national availability

- Whether listing is requested as an individual medicine or as an
  example of a therapeutic group

- Information supporting the public health relevance (epidemiological
  information on disease burden, assessment of current use, target
  population )

- Treatment details (dosage regimen, duration, reference to existing WHO
  and other clinical guidelines; need for special diagnostics, treatment
  or monitoring facilities and skills)

- Summary of comparative effectiveness in a variety of clinical
  settings:

  - Identification of clinical evidence (search

> strategy, systematic reviews identified, reasons for
> selection/exclusion of particular data)

- Summary of available data (appraisal of quality, outcome measures,
  summary of results)

<!-- -->

- Summary of comparative evidence on safety:

  - Estimate of total patient exposure to-date

  - Description of the adverse effects/ reactions and estimates of their
    frequency

  - Identification of variation in safety that may relate to health
    systems and patient factors

  - Summary of comparative safety against comparators.

- Summary of available data on comparative cost and cost- effectiveness
  within the pharmacological class or therapeutic group

  - range of costs of the proposed medicine

  - resource use and comparative cost-effectiveness presented as range
    of cost per routine outcome.

- Summary of regulatory status of the medicine (in various countries).
